## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling / materials science
**Analysis**: This task seeks a constitutive relationship between stress, strain, and temperature — a fundamental problem in materials science where stress depends on strain through elastic/plastic deformation laws and on temperature through thermal softening or thermally activated mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (linear elastic): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic regime, small strains)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - c2 * T) (linear elasticity with thermal softening of modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon equation for plastic strain hardening)
- Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Johnson-Cook strength (simplified): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T) (strain hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - (c3 * T)**c4) (homologous temperature softening)
- Voce hardening with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 - c1 * exp(-c2 * epsilon)) * (c3 - c4 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal term)
- Arrhenius-type thermal activation: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * (1/T)) (thermally activated deformation)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(-c2 * T) (power-law hardening with exponential softening)
- Swift equation with temperature: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * exp(-c3 * T) (shifted power law with thermal term)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (nonlinear elastic or hyperelastic approximation)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse form: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * epsilon**c2)**(-1) (stress with saturation at large strain)
- Hyperbolic sine creep law: sigma = c0 * asinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 * (1/T))) (sinh-based constitutive model)
- Combined power-exponential: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (power-law coupling of strain and temperature)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Strain hardening saturation → Use (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or Voce-type forms to capture stress plateaus at large strains
- Thermal softening of yield/flow stress → Multiplicative factor (1 - c*T^n) or exp(-c*T) applied to mechanical stress terms
- Thermally activated processes → Arrhenius-type exp(c/T) or exp(-c*T) terms reflecting dislocation mobility dependence on temperature
- Elastic-to-plastic transition → Additive decomposition: constant yield stress c0 plus strain-dependent hardening term c1*epsilon^c2
- Homologous temperature scaling → Temperature appears as normalized ratio (T - T_ref)/(T_melt - T_ref) raised to a power
- Strain offset for pre-existing defects → Replace epsilon with (epsilon + c) in power laws to avoid singularity at zero strain
- Separable strain-temperature structure → Stress factorizes as f(epsilon) * g(T), reflecting independent hardening and softening mechanisms
- Modulus-strain nonlinearity → Effective stiffness c0*(1 + c1*epsilon^c2) capturing nonlinear elastic or secant modulus behavior
